<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Word_order">Word order</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Breton_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Word order"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097763485">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+link+.ambox{margin-top:-1px}html body.mediawiki .mw-parser-output .ambox.mbox-small-left{margin:4px 1em 4px 0;overflow:hidden;width:238px;border-collapse:collapse;font-size:88%;line-height:1.25em}.mw-parser-output .ambox-speedy{border-left:10px solid #b32424;background-color:#fee7e6}.mw-parser-output .ambox-delete{border-left:10px solid #b32424}.mw-parser-output .ambox-content{border-left:10px solid #f28500}.mw-parser-output .ambox-style{border-left:10px solid #fc3}.mw-parser-output .ambox-move{border-left:10px solid #9932cc}.mw-parser-output .ambox-protection{border-left:10px solid #a2a9b1}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-text{border:none;padding:0.25em 0.5em;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-image{border:none;padding:2px 0 2px 0.5em;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-imageright{border:none;padding:2px 0.5em 2px 0;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-empty-cell{border:none;padding:0;width:1px}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-image-div{width:52px}html.client-js body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .mbox-text-span{margin-left:23px!important}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .ambox{margin:0 10%}}</style><table class="box-Expand_section plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="14" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31" /></a></span></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs expansion</b>&#32;with: V2 word order. You can help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Breton_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">May 2022</span>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Normal word order, like the other <a href="/wiki/Insular_Celtic_languages" title="Insular Celtic languages">Insular Celtic languages</a>, is at its core <a href="/wiki/Verb%E2%80%93subject%E2%80%93object_word_order" title="Verb–subject–object word order">VSO</a> (verb-subject-object), which is most apparent in embedded clauses. However, Breton finite verbs in <a href="/wiki/Main_clause" class="mw-redirect" title="Main clause">main clauses</a> are additionally subject to <a href="/wiki/V2_word_order" title="V2 word order">V2 word order</a> in which the finite main clause verb is typically the second element in the sentence.<sup id="cite_ref-V2_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-V2-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> That makes it perfectly possible to put the subject or the object at the beginning of the sentence, largely depending on the focus of the speaker. The following options are possible (all with a little difference in meaning):
</p>
<ul><li>the first places the verbal <a href="/wiki/Infinitive" title="Infinitive">infinitive</a> in initial position (as in (1)), followed by the <a href="/wiki/Auxiliary_verb" title="Auxiliary verb">auxiliary</a> <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">ober</i></span> 'to do'.</li>
<li>the second places the Auxiliary verb <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">bezañ</i></span> 'to be' in initial position (as in (2)), followed the Subject, and the construction <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">o(cʼh)</i></span> <i>+ infinitive</i>. At the end comes the Object. This construction is an exception to verb-second.</li>
<li>the third places the construction <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">o(cʼh)</i></span> <i>+ infinitive</i> in the initial position (as in (3)), followed by the Auxiliary verb <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">bezañ</i></span>, the Subject, and the Object.</li>
<li>the fourth option places the Object in initial position (as in (4)), followed by an inflected verb, followed by the Subject.</li>
<li>the fifth, and originally least common, places the Subject in initial position (as in (5)), followed by an inflected verb, followed by the Object, just like in English (SVO).</li></ul>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:4em"><div style="position:absolute;left:1em">(1)</div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Lenn</p><p style="margin: 0px;">read</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">a</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="preterite" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PRT</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ra</p><p style="margin: 0px;">do.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">brezhoneg</p><p style="margin: 0px;">Breton</p></div><p style="display: none;">Lenn a ra brezhoneg</p><p style="display: none;">read PRT do.3SG Breton</p><p style="clear: left;">'He/she reads Breton.'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:4em"><div style="position:absolute;left:1em">(2)</div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Ema</p><p style="margin: 0px;">be.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Yann</p><p style="margin: 0px;">Yann</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">o lenn</p><p style="margin: 0px;">reading</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">brezhoneg</p><p style="margin: 0px;">Breton</p></div><p style="display: none;">Ema Yann {o lenn} brezhoneg</p><p style="display: none;">be.3SG Yann reading Breton</p><p style="clear: left;">'Yann is reading Breton.'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:4em"><div style="position:absolute;left:1em">(3)</div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">O lenn</p><p style="margin: 0px;">reading</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ema</p><p style="margin: 0px;">be.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Yann</p><p style="margin: 0px;">Yann</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">brezhoneg</p><p style="margin: 0px;">Breton</p></div><p style="display: none;">{O lenn} ema Yann brezhoneg</p><p style="display: none;">reading be.3SG Yann Breton</p><p style="clear: left;">'Yann is reading Breton.'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:4em"><div style="position:absolute;left:1em">(4)</div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Mad</p><p style="margin: 0px;">good</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">eo</p><p style="margin: 0px;">be.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">an</p><p style="margin: 0px;">the</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">istor</p><p style="margin: 0px;">story</p></div><p style="display: none;">Mad eo an istor</p><p style="display: none;">good be.3SG the story</p><p style="clear: left;">'The story is good.'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:4em"><div style="position:absolute;left:1em">(5)</div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">An</p><p style="margin: 0px;">the</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">istor</p><p style="margin: 0px;">story</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">zo</p><p style="margin: 0px;">be.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person, singular" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3SG</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">mad</p><p style="margin: 0px;">good</p></div><p style="display: none;">An istor zo mad</p><p style="display: none;">the story be.3SG good</p><p style="clear: left;">'The story is good.'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Vocabulary">Vocabulary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Breton_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Vocabulary"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Breton uses much more borrowed vocabulary than its relatives further north; by some estimates a full 40% of its core vocabulary consists of loans from French.<sup id="cite_ref-Fortson_45-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fortson-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Orthography">Orthography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Breton_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Orthography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The first extant Breton texts, contained in the Leyde manuscript, were written at the end of the 8th century: 50 years prior to the <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg_Oaths" class="mw-redirect" title="Strasbourg Oaths">Strasbourg Oaths</a>, considered to be the earliest example of <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>. Like many medieval <a href="/wiki/Orthography" title="Orthography">orthographies</a>, Old- and Middle Breton orthography was at first not standardised, and the spelling of a particular word varied at authors' discretion. In 1499, however, the <i><a href="/wiki/Catholicon_(trilingual_dictionary)" title="Catholicon (trilingual dictionary)">Catholicon</a></i>, was published; as the first dictionary written for both French and Breton, it became a point of reference on how to transcribe the language. The orthography presented in the <i>Catholicon</i> was largely similar to that of French, in particular with respect to the representation of vowels, as well as the use of both the Latinate <a href="/wiki/Digraph_(orthography)" title="Digraph (orthography)">digraph</a> <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;qu&#x27e9;</span>—a remnant of the sound change <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kʷ/</span> &gt; <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/k/</span> in Latin—and Brittonic <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;cou-&#x27e9;</span> or <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;cu-&#x27e9;</span> to represent <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/k/</span> before front vowels.
</p><p>As phonetic and phonological differences between the dialects began to magnify, many regions, particularly the Vannes country, began to devise their own orthographies. Many of these orthographies were more closely related to the French model, albeit with some modifications. Examples of these modifications include the replacement of Old Breton -<span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;z&#x27e9;</span> with -<span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;h&#x27e9;</span> to denote word-final <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/x~h/</span> (an evolution of Old Breton <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/θ/</span> in the Vannes dialect) and use of -<span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;h&#x27e9;</span> to denote the initial mutation of <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/k/</span> (today this mutation is written <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;cʼh&#x27e9;</span>).<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> and thus needed another transcription.
</p><p>In the 1830s <a href="/wiki/Jean-Fran%C3%A7ois_Le_Gonidec" title="Jean-François Le Gonidec">Jean-François Le Gonidec</a> created a modern phonetic system for the language.
</p><p>During the early years of the 20th century, a group of writers known as <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">Emglev ar Skrivanerien</i></span> elaborated and reformed Le Gonidec's system. They made it more suitable as a super-dialectal representation of the dialects of <a href="/wiki/Cornouaille" title="Cornouaille">Cornouaille</a>, Leon and Trégor (known as from <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">Kernev</i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">Leon</i></span> and <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">Treger</i></span> in Breton). This <b>KLT</b> orthography was established in 1911. At the same time writers of the more divergent Vannetais dialect developed a phonetic system also based on that of Le Gonidec.
</p><p>Following proposals made during the 1920s, the KLT and Vannetais orthographies were merged in 1941 to create an orthographic system to represent all four dialects. This <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">Peurunvan</i></span> ("wholly unified") orthography was significant for the inclusion of the digraph <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;zh&#x27e9;</span>, which represents a <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/h/</span> in Vannetais and corresponds to a <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/z/</span> in the KLT dialects.
</p><p>In 1955 <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Falc%CA%BChun" title="François Falcʼhun">François Falcʼhun</a> and the group Emgleo Breiz proposed a new orthography. It was designed to use a set of <a href="/wiki/Graphemes" class="mw-redirect" title="Graphemes">graphemes</a> closer to the conventions of French. This <span title="French-language text"><i lang="fr">Orthographe universitaire</i></span> ("University Orthography", known in Breton as <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">Skolveurieg</i></span>) was given official recognition by the French authorities as the "official orthography of Breton in French education." It was opposed in the region and today is used only by the magazine <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">Brud Nevez</i></span> and the publishing house Emgléo Breiz.
</p><p>In the 1970s, a new standard orthography was devised — the <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">etrerannyezhel</i></span> or <span title="French-language text"><i lang="fr">interdialectale</i></span>. This system is based on the derivation of the words.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Today the majority of writers continue to use the <i>Peurunvan orthography</i>, and it is the version taught in most Breton-language schools.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alphabet">Alphabet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Breton_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Alphabet"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Breton is written in the <a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">Latin script</a>. <i>Peurunvan</i>, the most commonly used orthography, consists of the following letters:
</p>
<dl><dd>a, b, ch, cʼh, d, e, f, g, h, i, j, k, l, m, n, o, p, r, s, t, u, v, w, y, z</dd></dl>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Circumflex" title="Circumflex">circumflex</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grave_accent" title="Grave accent">grave accent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trema_(diacritic)" class="mw-redirect" title="Trema (diacritic)">trema</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tilde" title="Tilde">tilde</a> appear on some letters. These <a href="/wiki/Diacritic" title="Diacritic">diacritics</a> are used in the following way:
</p>
<dl><dd>â, ê, î, ô, û, ù, ü, ñ</dd></dl>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Differences_between_Skolveurieg_and_Peurunvan">Differences between <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">Skolveurieg</i></span> and <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">Peurunvan</i></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Breton_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Differences between Skolveurieg and Peurunvan"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Both orthographies use the above alphabet, although <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;é&#x27e9;</span> is used only in <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">Skolveurieg</i></span>.
</p><p>Differences between the two systems are particularly noticeable in word endings. In Peurunvan, final <a href="/wiki/Obstruent" title="Obstruent">obstruents</a>, which are devoiced in absolute final position and voiced in <a href="/wiki/Sandhi" title="Sandhi">sandhi</a> before voiced sounds, are represented by a grapheme that indicates a voiceless sound. In OU they are written as voiced but represented as voiceless before suffixes: <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">braz</i></span> "big", <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">brasocʼh</i></span> "bigger".
</p><p>In addition, Peurunvan maintains the KLT convention, which distinguishes noun/adjective pairs by nouns written with a final voiced consonant and adjectives with a voiceless one. No distinction is made in pronunciation, e.g. <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">brezhoneg</i></span> "Breton language" vs. <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">brezhonek</i></span> "Breton (adj)".
</p>

<p><b>Notes:</b>
</p>
<ol><li><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1041539562">.mw-parser-output .citation{word-wrap:break-word}.mw-parser-output .citation:target{background-color:rgba(0,127,255,0.133)}</style><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Pron-1"><b><a href="#ref_Pron-1">^</a></b></span>  Vocative particle: <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">â Vreizh</i></span> "O Brittany".</li>
<li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Pron-2"><b><a href="#ref_Pron-2">^</a></b></span>  Word-initially.</li>
<li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Pron-3"><b><a href="#ref_Pron-3">^</a></b></span>  Word-finally.</li>
<li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Pron-4"><b><a href="#ref_Pron-4">^</a></b></span>  Unwritten lenition of <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;ch, cʼh, f, s&#x27e9;</span> and spirantization of <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;p&#x27e9;</span> &gt; <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;f&#x27e9;</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[v]</span>.</li>
<li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Pron-5"><b><a href="#ref_Pron-5">^</a></b></span>  Unstressed <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;e, eu, o&#x27e9;</span> represent <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɛ,<span class="wrap"> </span>œ,<span class="wrap"> </span>ɔ]</span> in Leoneg but <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[e,<span class="wrap"> </span>ø,<span class="wrap"> </span>o]</span> in the other dialects. The realisations <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɛ̞,<span class="wrap"> </span>œ̞,<span class="wrap"> </span>ɔ̞]</span> appear mainly before <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;rr&#x27e9;</span> (also less often before <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;cʼh&#x27e9;</span>), semivowels <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[j,<span class="wrap"> </span>w]</span>, consonant clusters beginning with <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;r&#x27e9;</span> or <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;l&#x27e9;</span>. Stressed long <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;e, eu, o&#x27e9;</span> represent <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[eː,<span class="wrap"> </span>øː,<span class="wrap"> </span>oː]</span>.</li>
<li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Pron-6"><b><a href="#ref_Pron-6">^</a></b></span>  In Gwenedeg velars are palatalized before <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;e&#x27e9;</span> and <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;i&#x27e9;</span>, i.e. <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;k&#x27e9;</span>, <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;g&#x27e9;</span>, <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;kw/kou&#x27e9;</span>, <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;cʼhw/cʼhou&#x27e9;</span>, <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;gw/gou&#x27e9;</span>, <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;w/ou&#x27e9;</span>, <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;sk&#x27e9;</span> represent <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[c~tʃ,<span class="wrap"> </span>ɟ~dʒ,<span class="wrap"> </span>cɥ,<span class="wrap"> </span>hɥ,<span class="wrap"> </span>ɟɥ,<span class="wrap"> </span>ɥ,<span class="wrap"> </span>sc~ʃc]</span>. In the case of word-final <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;g&#x27e9;</span> and <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;k&#x27e9;</span> palatalization to <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[c]</span> also occurs after <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;i&#x27e9;</span>.</li>
<li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Pron-7"><b><a href="#ref_Pron-7">^</a></b></span>  Before a vowel other than <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;i&#x27e9;</span> the digraph <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;ni&#x27e9;</span> is written instead of <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;gn&#x27e9;</span>, e.g. <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">bleniañ</i></span> "to drive", radical <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">blegn</i></span>, 1PS preterite <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">blegnis</i></span>, 3PS preterite <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">blenias</i></span>.</li>
<li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Pron-8"><b><a href="#ref_Pron-8">^</a></b></span>  Silent in words such as <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br"><b>h</b>a(g)</i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br"><b>h</b>e(cʼh)</i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br"><b>h</b>o(cʼh)</i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br"><b>h</b>oll</i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br"><b>h</b>on</i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br"><b>h</b>or</i></span> and <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br"><b>h</b>ol</i></span>. Always silent in Gwenedeg and Leoneg.</li>
<li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Pron-9"><b><a href="#ref_Pron-9">^</a></b></span>  <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;i&#x27e9;</span> is realized as <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[j]</span> when it precedes or follows a vowel (or when between vowels), but in words such as <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">l<b>i</b>en</i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">l<b>i</b>orzh</i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">rakd<b>i</b>azezañ</i></span> it represents <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[iː]</span> (in orthography <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;ï&#x27e9;</span> may be used: <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">lïen</i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">lïorzh</i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">rakdïazezañ</i></span>).</li>
<li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Pron-10"><b><a href="#ref_Pron-10">^</a></b></span>  <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;ilh&#x27e9;</span> represents <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ʎ]</span> when it follows a vowel, after a consonant it represents <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[iʎ]</span>. But before a vowel other than <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;i&#x27e9;</span>, <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;li&#x27e9;</span> is written instead of <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;ilh&#x27e9;</span>, e.g. <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">heuliañ</i></span> "to follow", radical <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">heuilh</i></span>, 1PS preterite <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">heuilhis</i></span>, 3PS preterite <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">heulias</i></span>. In some regions <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[j]</span> may be heard instead of <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ʎ]</span>.</li>
<li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Pron-11"><b><a href="#ref_Pron-11">^</a></b></span>  Word-finally after a cluster of unvoiced consonants.</li>
<li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Pron-12"><b><a href="#ref_Pron-12">^</a></b></span>  In front of <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;k, g&#x27e9;</span>.</li>
<li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Pron-13"><b><a href="#ref_Pron-13">^</a></b></span>  The digraph <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;ou&#x27e9;</span> is realized like <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;w&#x27e9;</span> when preceded or followed by a vowel (or when between vowels), but in words such as <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">Doue</i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">douar</i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">gouarn</i></span> it represents <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[uː]</span>.</li>
<li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Pron-14"><b><a href="#ref_Pron-14">^</a></b></span>  The digraph <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;où&#x27e9;</span> represents plural endings. Its pronunciation varies by dialect: <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[u,<span class="wrap"> </span>o,<span class="wrap"> </span>ø,<span class="wrap"> </span>ow,<span class="wrap"> </span>aw,<span class="wrap"> </span>aɥ,<span class="wrap"> </span>ɔɥ]</span> rating geographically from Northwest Leon to Southeast Gwened.</li>
<li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Pron-15"><b><a href="#ref_Pron-15">^</a></b></span>  <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;v&#x27e9;</span> usually represents <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[v]</span>, but word-finally (except in word-final <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;ñv&#x27e9;</span>) it represents <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[w]</span> in KLT, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɥ]</span> in Gwenedeg and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[f]</span> in Goëlo. The pronunciation <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[v]</span> is retained word-finally in verbs. In words <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">bli<b>v</b></i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">Gwiskri<b>v</b></i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">gwi<b>v</b></i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">li<b>v</b></i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">pi<b>v</b></i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">ri<b>v</b></i></span> it represents <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[u]</span> in KLT, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɥ]</span> in Gwenedeg and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[f]</span> in Goëlo. Word-finally following <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;r, l, n, z&#x27e9;</span> it represents <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[o]</span>.</li>
<li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Pron-16"><b><a href="#ref_Pron-16">^</a></b></span>  But silent in words such as <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">goue<b>z</b></i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">bloa<b>z</b></i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">goa<b>z</b></i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">ru<b>z</b>iañ</i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">klei<b>z</b></i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">rakdïaze<b>z</b>añ</i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">be<b>z</b>añ</i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">Roa<b>zh</b>on</i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">de<b>zh</b>añ</i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">koue<b>zh</b>añ</i></span>, '<span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br"><b>z</b></i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">a<b>z</b></i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">e<b>z</b></i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">da'</i></span><span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br"><b>z</b></i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">gwirione<b>z</b></i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">enep(g)wirione<b>z</b></i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">monei<b>z</b></i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">falsvonei<b>z</b></i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">karante<b>z</b></i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">kengarante<b>z</b></i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">neve<b>z</b></i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">neve<b>z</b>cʼhanet</i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">nado<b>z</b>ioù</i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">abardae<b>z</b></i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">gwe<b>z</b></i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">bemde<b>z</b></i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">kri<b>z</b></i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">blei<b>z</b></i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">morvlei<b>z</b></i></span>, <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">de<b>zh</b>i</i></span>. <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;z&#x27e9;</span> is generally silent in Kerneweg, Tregerieg and Gwenedeg, but in Leoneg <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;z(h)&#x27e9;</span> is always pronounced.</li>
<li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Pron-17"><b><a href="#ref_Pron-17">^</a></b></span>  Used to distinguish words such as <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">stêr</i></span> "river", <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">hêr</i></span> "heir", <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">kêr</i></span> "town" (also written <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">kaer</i></span>) from <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">ster</i></span> "sense", <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">her</i></span> "bold", <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">ker</i></span> "dear".</li>
<li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Pron-18"><b><a href="#ref_Pron-18">^</a></b></span>  Used to distinguish <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">trôad</i></span> "circuit/tour" from <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">troad</i></span> "foot".</li>
<li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Pron-19"><b><a href="#ref_Pron-19">^</a></b></span>  In northern dialects (mainly in Leoneg), there is a tendency to voice <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;cʼh&#x27e9;</span> between vowels. <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɣ]</span> also appears as the lenition of <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;g, cʼh&#x27e9;</span> and mixed mutation of <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;g&#x27e9;</span>.</li>
<li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Pron-20"><b><a href="#ref_Pron-20">^</a></b></span>  The lenition of <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;d&#x27e9;</span> and the spirantization of <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;t&#x27e9;</span> are both represented by <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;z&#x27e9;</span> is mainly pronounced <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[z]</span> although in certain regions <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[s]</span> (especially for the spirantization of <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;t&#x27e9;</span> in Cornouaille) and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ð]</span> (in some Haut-Vannetais varieties)<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Pron-31"><a href="#endnote_Pron-31">31</a></sup> also occur.</li>
<li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Pron-21"><b><a href="#ref_Pron-21">^</a></b></span>  The pronunciation of <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;r&#x27e9;</span> varies by dialect, nowadays uvular <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ʀ]</span> (or <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ʁ]</span>) is standard; <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[r]</span> occurs in Leoneg, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɾ]</span> or <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɹ]</span> in Tregerieg, and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ʀ],<span class="wrap"> </span>[ʁ],<span class="wrap"> </span>[r],<span class="wrap"> </span>and<span class="wrap"> </span>[ɾ]</span> in Gwenedeg.</li>
<li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Pron-22"><b><a href="#ref_Pron-22">^</a></b></span>  In Gwenedeg an unstressed <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;e&#x27e9;</span> often represents <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ə]</span>.</li>
<li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Pron-23"><b><a href="#ref_Pron-23">^</a></b></span>  Lenited varieties of <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;r, l, n&#x27e9;</span> may appear word-initially in case of soft mutation.</li>
<li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Pron-24"><b><a href="#ref_Pron-24">^</a></b></span>  In Leoneg <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[u(ː)]</span> in front of a nasal.</li>
<li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Pron-25"><b><a href="#ref_Pron-25">^</a></b></span>  In Leoneg <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;w&#x27e9;</span> represents <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[v]</span> before <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;e, i&#x27e9;</span>.</li>
<li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Pron-26"><b><a href="#ref_Pron-26">^</a></b></span>  In Leoneg <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;z(h)&#x27e9;</span> represents <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ʃ]</span> or <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ʒ]</span> before <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;i&#x27e9;</span>.</li>
<li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Pron-27"><b><a href="#ref_Pron-27">^</a></b></span>  In Leoneg <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;gwr&#x27e9;</span> represents <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɡr]</span>.</li>
<li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Pron-28"><b><a href="#ref_Pron-28">^</a></b></span>  Before a vowel.</li>
<li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Pron-29"><b><a href="#ref_Pron-29">^</a></b></span>  Forms of the indefinite article.</li>
<li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1041539562"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Pron-30"><b><a href="#ref_Pron-30">^</a></b></span>  A conservative realisation of the initial mutation of <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;d&#x27e9;</span> and <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;t&#x27e9;</span>, used in certain parts of the Vannes country.</li></ol>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sample_texts">Sample texts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Breton_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Sample texts"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><b>Article 1 of the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">Universal Declaration of Human Rights</a></b>
</p>
<table>

<tbody><tr>
<td><b>Breton</b>: <br /><span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">Dieub ha par en o dellezegezh hag o gwirioù eo ganet an holl dud. Poell ha skiant zo dezho ha dleout a reont bevañ an eil gant egile en ur spered a genvreudeuriezh.</i></span><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</td>
<td style="padding-left: 1em"><b>English</b>: <br /> All human beings are born free and equal in dignity and rights. They are endowed with reason and conscience and should act towards one another in a spirit of brotherhood.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h3><span id="Lord.27s_Prayer"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Lord's_Prayer">Lord's Prayer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Breton_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Lord&#039;s Prayer"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<dl><dd><i>Hon Tad,</i></dd>
<dd><i>cʼhwi hag a zo en Neñv,</i></dd>
<dd><i>ra vo santelaet hocʼh anv.</i></dd>
<dd><i>Ra zeuio ho Rouantelezh.</i></dd>
<dd><i>Ra vo graet ho youl war an douar evel en neñv.</i></dd>
<dd><i>Roit dimp hiziv bara hor bevañs.</i></dd>
<dd><i>Distaolit dimp hon dleoù</i></dd>
<dd><i>evel m'hor bo ivez distaolet d'hon dleourion.</i></dd>
<dd><i>Ha n'hon lezit ket da vont gant an temptadur,</i></dd>
<dd><i>met hon dieubit eus an Droug.</i></dd></dl>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Words_and_phrases_in_Breton">Words and phrases in Breton</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Breton_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Words and phrases in Breton"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Road_signs_bilingual_Breton_in_Quimper.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Road_signs_bilingual_Breton_in_Quimper.jpg/220px-Road_signs_bilingual_Breton_in_Quimper.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="238" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Road_signs_bilingual_Breton_in_Quimper.jpg/330px-Road_signs_bilingual_Breton_in_Quimper.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Road_signs_bilingual_Breton_in_Quimper.jpg/440px-Road_signs_bilingual_Breton_in_Quimper.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1037" data-file-height="1120" /></a><figcaption>Bilingual signage in <a href="/wiki/Quimper/Kemper" class="mw-redirect" title="Quimper/Kemper">Quimper/Kemper</a>. Note the use of the word <i>ti</i> in the Breton for <i>police station</i> and <i>tourist office</i>, plus <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">da bep lecʼh</i></span> for <i>all directions</i>.</figcaption></figure>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Borrowing_from_Breton_by_other_languages">Borrowing from Breton by other languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Breton_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Borrowing from Breton by other languages"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The English words <span title="English-language text"><span lang="en">dolmen</span></span> and <span title="English-language text"><span lang="en"><a href="/wiki/Menhir" title="Menhir">menhir</a></span></span> have been borrowed from French, which took them from Breton. However, this is uncertain: for instance, <span title="English-language text"><span lang="en">menhir</span></span> is <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">peulvan</i></span> or <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">maen hir</i></span> ("long stone"), <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">maen sav</i></span> ("straight stone") (two words: noun + adjective) in Breton. <i>Dolmen</i> is a misconstructed word (it should be <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">taol-<b>v</b>aen</i></span>). Some studies state<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> that these words were borrowed from <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>. <span title="Welsh-language text"><i lang="cy">Maen hir</i></span> can be directly translated from Welsh as "long stone" (which is exactly what a <span title="English-language text"><span lang="en">menhir</span></span> or <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">maen hir</i></span> is). The Cornish surnames Mennear, Minear and Manhire all derive from the Cornish <span title="Cornish-language text"><i lang="kw">men</i></span> <span title="Cornish-language text"><i lang="kw">hyr</i></span> ("long stone"), as does <span title="Cornish-language text"><i lang="kw">Tremenheere</i></span> "settlement by the long stone".
</p><p>The French word <span title="French-language text"><i lang="fr">baragouiner</i></span> ("to jabber in a foreign language") is derived from Breton <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">bara</i></span> ("bread") and <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">gwin</i></span> ("wine"). The French word <span title="French-language text"><i lang="fr">goéland</i></span> ("large seagull") is derived from Breton <span title="Breton-language text"><i lang="br">gwelan</i></span>, which shares the same root as English "gull" (Welsh <span title="Welsh-language text"><i lang="cy">gwylan</i></span>, Cornish <span title="Cornish-language text"><i lang="kw">goelann</i></span>).
</p>

<li id="cite_note-Fortson-45"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Fortson_45-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Fortson_45-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Fortson_45-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Fortson_45-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Fortson_45-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Fortson_45-5"><sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Fortson_45-6"><sup><i><b>g</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Fortson, Benjamin W. 2005. <i>Indo-European Language and Culture</i>. Page 295: "Breton has also borrowed much more heavily from French throughout its history than any of the other British Celtic languages ever have from English, to the extent that two-fifths of the ordinary vocabulary is of French origin, according to some extents".</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-V2-46"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-V2_46-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1133582631"><cite id="CITEREFKennard2018" class="citation journal cs1">Kennard, Holly J. (12 January 2018). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://ora.ox.ac.uk/objects/uuid:9131b11a-3eff-43b1-9055-b6c9f19b413b">"Non-Negative Word Order In Breton: Maintaining Verb-Second"</a>. <i>Transactions of the Philological Society</i>. Wiley. <b>116</b> (2): 153–178. <a href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1111%2F1467-968x.12119">10.1111/1467-968x.12119</a>. <a href="/wiki/ISSN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISSN (identifier)">ISSN</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.worldcat.org/issn/0079-1636">0079-1636</a>. <a href="/wiki/S2CID_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="S2CID (identifier)">S2CID</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://api.semanticscholar.org/CorpusID:148910543">148910543</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Transactions+of+the+Philological+Society&amp;rft.atitle=Non-Negative+Word+Order+In+Breton%3A+Maintaining+Verb-Second&amp;rft.volume=116&amp;rft.issue=2&amp;rft.pages=153-178&amp;rft.date=2018-01-12&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fapi.semanticscholar.org%2FCorpusID%3A148910543%23id-name%3DS2CID&amp;rft.issn=0079-1636&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1111%2F1467-968x.12119&amp;rft.aulast=Kennard&amp;rft.aufirst=Holly+J.&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fora.ox.ac.uk%2Fobjects%2Fuuid%3A9131b11a-3eff-43b1-9055-b6c9f19b413b&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABreton+language" class="Z3988"></span></span>

<p><b>Dictionaries</b>
</p>
<ul><li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20120120125126/http://www.etymos.de/us/languages/breton/index.htm">English online dictionary and grammar for Breton</a></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.langtolang.com/">A multilingual dictionary containing many Breton words alongside those of other languages</a></li></ul>
<p><b>Learning</b>
</p>
<ul><li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20140704082247/http://www.kervarker.org/index.php?newlang=english%2F">Breton site including online lessons</a></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.linguashop.com/breton-language/">Audio CD, workbooks, software in English to learn Breton</a></li>
<li>Breton site with learners' forum and lessons (mostly in French with some English)</li>
<li>Jouitteau, M. <i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://arbres.iker.cnrs.fr/index.php/Grammaire_du_breton">Grammaire du breton</a></i>, (extensive Breton grammar in French, with glossed examples and typological comparisons), IKER, CNRS, 2009 &gt; 2017].</li></ul>
